    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12873335807367823983">Adolf Hitler: My Part on His Downfall is volume One of Spike Milligan's outrageous, hilarious, legendary War Memoirs.<br/><br/>'At Victoria station the R.T.O. gave me a travel warrant, a white feather and a picture of Hitler marked "This is your enemy". I searched every compartment, but he wasn't on the train . . .'<br/><br/>In this, the first of Spike Milligan's uproarious recollections of l</span>
  <span id="freeText12873335807367823983" style="display:none">Adolf Hitler: My Part on His Downfall is volume One of Spike Milligan's outrageous, hilarious, legendary War Memoirs.<br /><br />'At Victoria station the R.T.O. gave me a travel warrant, a white feather and a picture of Hitler marked "This is your enemy". I searched every compartment, but he wasn't on the train . . .'<br /><br />In this, the first of Spike Milligan's uproarious recollections of life in the army, our hero takes us from the outbreak of war in 1939 ('it must have been something we said'), through his attempts to avoid enlistment ('time for my appendicitus, I thought') and his gunner training in Bexhill ('There was one drawback. No ammunition') to the landing at Algiers in 1943 ('I closed my eyes and faced the sun. I fell down a hatchway').<br /><br />Filled with bathos, pathos and gales of ribald laughter, this is a barely sane helping of military goonery and superlative Milliganese.<br /><br />'The most irreverent, hilarious book about the war that I have ever read' Sunday Express<br /><br />'Desperately funny, vivid, vulgar' Sunday Times<br /><br />'Milligan is the Great God to all of us' John Cleese<br /><br />'The Godfather of Alternative Comedy' Eddie Izzard<br /><br />'That absolutely glorious way of looking at things differently. A great man' Stephen Fry<br /><br />Spike Milligan was one of the greatest and most influential comedians of the twentieth century. Born in India in 1918, he served in the Royal Artillery during WWII in North Africa and Italy. At the end of the war, he forged a career as a jazz musician, sketch-show writer and performer, before joining forces with Peter Sellers and Harry Secombe to form the legendary Goon Show. Until his death in 2002, he had success as on stage and screen and as the author of over eighty books of fiction, memoir, poetry, plays, cartoons and children's stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12873335807367823983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1361697269" />
    <a title="Paul E. Morph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44824883-paul-e-morph"><img alt="Paul E. Morph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602970987p2/44824883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1361697269?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul E. Morph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul E. Morph" href="/user/show/44824883-paul-e-morph">Paul E. Morph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780718108663" href="/book/show/2721449-adolf-hitler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44824883-paul-e-morph?shelf=books-read-in-2017">books-read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1361697269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11006298834715948324">Oh, holy crap... I can't breathe! My neighbours probably think I've gone completely off my trolley as I've spent most of this book laughing very much out loud!<br/><br/>This is a re-read for me; I think I read it for the first time in paperback about a decade ago, but when I saw the Scribd e-library had all seven volumes in audiobook format read by the man himself, I couldn't resist reading them again. I'm actually not entirely sure how many volumes of this I read the first time around but I'm pretty sure</span>
  <span id="freeText11006298834715948324" style="display:none">Oh, holy crap... I can't breathe! My neighbours probably think I've gone completely off my trolley as I've spent most of this book laughing very much out loud!<br /><br />This is a re-read for me; I think I read it for the first time in paperback about a decade ago, but when I saw the Scribd e-library had all seven volumes in audiobook format read by the man himself, I couldn't resist reading them again. I'm actually not entirely sure how many volumes of this I read the first time around but I'm pretty sure it wasn't all seven. I'm definitely going all the way this time, though.<br /><br />This has to be one of the funniest war memoirs ever written. Spike brings his trademark manic eye to bear on his own experiences as a gunner in World War II and, while some of the events are tragic (obviously) you still barely get a chance to breathe between laughs.<br /><br />Yes, it's irreverent, yes, it's disrespectful, but laughing in the face of tragedy is how we Brits keep from going insane. You'd have to be a seriously curmudgeonly bugger not to crack a smile reading this.<br /><br />Right! Bring on volume two!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11006298834715948324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_6630533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6630533" />
    <a title="Telesilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/319699-telesilla"><img alt="Telesilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390999826p2/319699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6630533?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Telesilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Telesilla" href="/user/show/319699-telesilla">Telesilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/319699-telesilla?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6630533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11735871953949750548">Recently when I posted a quote from this book, people guessed that it came from Terry Prachett or Monty Python or Douglas Adams. Which is actually rather revealing because if modern British comedy and humor writers have a spiritual grandfather, it's Spike Milligan. Although he was also a talented musician, he became known for his mad cap and often surreal comedy writing, particularly his work on the Goon Show.<br/><br/>Before all that, he went to war, and before he went to war, he had to be trained. This </span>
  <span id="freeText11735871953949750548" style="display:none">Recently when I posted a quote from this book, people guessed that it came from Terry Prachett or Monty Python or Douglas Adams. Which is actually rather revealing because if modern British comedy and humor writers have a spiritual grandfather, it's Spike Milligan. Although he was also a talented musician, he became known for his mad cap and often surreal comedy writing, particularly his work on the Goon Show.<br /><br />Before all that, he went to war, and before he went to war, he had to be trained. This book, the first in a series, looks at the time he spent with his unit wandering around Southern Britain learning how to soldier, and it's hilarious. From the bizarre officer's dances Spike's band played at to the crazy antics they got up to when learning to work the radios--he was a radio operator--it's funny in a slightly crazed way. Milligan actually suffered from bi-polar disorder all his life, and this whole book reads like an extended and very funny up period.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11735871953949750548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15728962961096649292" style="display:none"><b>Spike Milligan's personal wartime memories<br>Censors warning Non P.C. language</b><br><br>image: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1568091368i/28125302.jpg" width="400" height="275" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At Victoria Station the R.T.O. gave me a travel warrant, a white feather and a picture of Hitler marked ‘This is your enemy’. That night, in bed, surrounded by the Enemy, I ate my Emergency Chocolate.<br><br><i>In Algeria</i><br>I made friends with two little French kids on their way to school, a girl and a boy. I gave them two English pennies. In exchange they gave me an empty matchbox, with a camel label on the top. I shall always remember their faces.<br><br><b>Savor a view of World War Two from one member of Britain's best comedy team - The Goons</b><br><br>Enjoy!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5259796952962899228"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6041352.Adolf_Hitler_My_Part_in_his_Downfall' title='Adolf Hitler My Part in his Downfall by Spike Milligan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Adolf Hitler: My Part in his Downfall</a>, is the first of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/114722.Spike_Milligan' title='Spike Milligan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Spike Milligan</a>'s seven memoirs that recount his recollections of life in the army during World War 2. I read this book as a teenager in the mid-1970s (or, put another way, a very long time ago) and I loved it and have always meant to read it again. It was even better than I had remembered. <br/><br/>For all the privations of army life, it is clear that Spike had a lot of fun during this period, and the humour that was to make his name with the Goons a</span>
  <span id="freeText5259796952962899228" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6041352.Adolf_Hitler_My_Part_in_his_Downfall" title="Adolf Hitler My Part in his Downfall by Spike Milligan" rel="nofollow noopener">Adolf Hitler: My Part in his Downfall</a>, is the first of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/114722.Spike_Milligan" title="Spike Milligan" rel="nofollow noopener">Spike Milligan</a>'s seven memoirs that recount his recollections of life in the army during World War 2. I read this book as a teenager in the mid-1970s (or, put another way, a very long time ago) and I loved it and have always meant to read it again. It was even better than I had remembered. <br><br>For all the privations of army life, it is clear that Spike had a lot of fun during this period, and the humour that was to make his name with the Goons and beyond is here in abundance. That said, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6041352.Adolf_Hitler_My_Part_in_his_Downfall" title="Adolf Hitler My Part in his Downfall by Spike Milligan" rel="nofollow noopener">Adolf Hitler: My Part in his Downfall</a> ends just as Spike's regiment arrives in Algiers for its first taste of action and, whilst there is some tragedy in this memoir, things will inevitably get more serious from here on in. <br><br>Spike's silliness is infectious and the book contains a winning combination of word play, self deprecating humour and social history. And, a very credible evocation, of the life of a conscript at the start of the war right down to the smelliness of the army uniforms and how nobody got the correct size. The book contains plenty of surprising and frequently outrageous anecdotes, many of which are loud out loud funny. <br><br>4/5<br><br>The entire series is...<br><br>Adolf Hitler: My Part in His Downfall (1971)<br>"Rommel?" "Gunner Who?" (1974)<br>Monty: His Part in My Victory (1976) <br>Mussolini: His Part in My Downfall (1978)<br>Where Have All the Bullets Gone? (1985)<br>Goodbye Soldier (1986)<br>Peace Work (1992)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400162350i/9642886.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Spike Milligan (1918 - 2002) is described on his gravestone as 'Writer, Artist, Musician, Humanitarian, Comedian'.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9780241966150" href="/book/show/18922365-adolf-hitler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31913163-cathal-kenneally?shelf=2018-reading-challenge">2018-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2382022516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15924976061704669817"><strong>Brilliant!</strong><br/><br/>I was shown a picture of Adolf Hitler and was told ,this is your enemy. I searched every compartment of the train but I couldn't find him anywhere. If this isn't enough to rope you in then I don't know what is. It piqued my curiosity immediately. A brilliant take of life during wartime. Having to enlist when most people probably didn't want to. He has included fictional characters throughout, just as well! The humour remains the same. Typically Milligan to the end.😂</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_936197654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/936197654" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/936197654?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9780241966150" href="/book/show/18922365-adolf-hitler">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer936197654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4994970641496960180">This is an utterly surreal, joyous and irreverent look at Spike Milligan’s time as a young soldier in WWII. This book takes us from the outbreak of war through to the beginning of 1943 when Milligan arrives in Algiers. In between there is receiving his call up papers, endless training – none of which he appears to have had any aptitude for – and his first steps into ‘Show Business’ when he teams up with fellow jazz fans to play at dances.<br/><br/>As Milligan himself states in the introduction, many terri</span>
  <span id="freeText4994970641496960180" style="display:none">This is an utterly surreal, joyous and irreverent look at Spike Milligan’s time as a young soldier in WWII. This book takes us from the outbreak of war through to the beginning of 1943 when Milligan arrives in Algiers. In between there is receiving his call up papers, endless training – none of which he appears to have had any aptitude for – and his first steps into ‘Show Business’ when he teams up with fellow jazz fans to play at dances.<br /><br />As Milligan himself states in the introduction, many terrible things happened in the war, but humour helped him cope. The names, whether made up or real, are straight from a Waugh novel – Battery Sergeant-Major ‘Jumbo’ Day for example could easily have been a character in “Men at Arms”. Everything is taken with humour and Milligan is full of wonderfully bad puns – when he finds that, during a romantic tryst in a lorry, somebody drives off with them on board, he returns to his friends who ask where he disappeared to, replying, “I got carried away...”<br /><br />I am amazed it took me so long to get around to reading Spike Milligan’s war memoirs, but I am truly glad that there are many more books to read. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4994970641496960180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

When his friend points out there are only two of them his solution, "We'll sit a long way apart!" Just loved </span>
  <span id="freeText14929709038967722101" style="display:none">It has been so long since I laughed out aloud reading a book. Spike Milligan is hilarious. I kept my daughter awake for nights on end - we shared a bed while her dad was away. She asked me to read out what I was reading but didn't quite "get it". She is only 12 but my guess is that humour is different for everyone. I loved his one-liners, his suggestion to a friend that they form a band. When his friend points out there are only two of them his solution, "We'll sit a long way apart!" Just loved it. A genius. I must read more of his works now. Highly recommended.</span>

I searched every compartment, but he wasn't on the train. At 4.30, June 2nd, 1940, on a summer's day all mare's tails and blue sky we arrived at Bexhill-on-Sea, where I got off. It wasn't easy.   <span id="freeText4646119101247533505" style="display:none"><blockquote><br />At Victoria Station the R.T.O. gave me a travel warrant, a white feather and a picture of Hitler marked 'This is your enemy'. I searched every compartment, but he wasn't on the train. At 4.30, June 2nd, 1940, on a summer's day all mare's tails and blue sky we arrived at Bexhill-on-Sea, where I got off. It wasn't easy. The train didn't stop there.<br /></blockquote><br /><br />Before Spike Milligan wrote The Goon Show he had to go to war. He wrote seven short books about the experience based on his diaries, here's the first one which concerns joining the army, training, starting a jazz band during training, more training, exploits/hijinks/affairs, and finally getting shipped off to Northern Africa, where the book ends.<br /><br />Roughly every third sentence is a joke, and most are good - sometimes, randomly, the horrors and insanity of his situation creeps in for a paragraph where he describes (without joking) how a fellow soldier died in an accident, or how decades later he visited the same place and cannot deal with the ghosts ('What’s happened to us all since then? The world’s gone sour. Happiness is a yesterday thing.')<br /><br />I don't know if this is for everyone, did the first paragraph made you laugh? Then go for it, it's like that the entire time.<br /><br /><blockquote><br />Occasions of insanity such as this stopped us all going mad.<br /></blockquote></span>

    <a title="Rich Meyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4585903-rich-meyer"><img alt="Rich Meyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442485356p2/4585903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer220832734" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer702367623873284897">This is a very funny book. It was a little hard to get into at first, given the colloquialisms that Milligan is wont to use, but you get used to it fairly quickly (at least I did, being an American who's an Anglophile at heart). The humor is pithy and nearly constant, but there's a good look into what was happening in Britain in the early days of World War II, which is entirely different from the picture most of us have of the US during the same period, since beyond Pearl Harbor, none of us had </span>
  <span id="freeText702367623873284897" style="display:none">This is a very funny book. It was a little hard to get into at first, given the colloquialisms that Milligan is wont to use, but you get used to it fairly quickly (at least I did, being an American who's an Anglophile at heart). The humor is pithy and nearly constant, but there's a good look into what was happening in Britain in the early days of World War II, which is entirely different from the picture most of us have of the US during the same period, since beyond Pearl Harbor, none of us had to worry about the major enemy forces attacking us personally every day. <br /><br />I'm hoping to start the next book in the series soon.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2539488757" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2539488757" />
    <a title="Zoeb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78712152-zoeb"><img alt="Zoeb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520855238p2/78712152.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2539488757?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoeb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoeb" href="/user/show/78712152-zoeb">Zoeb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539488757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4339501542981988012">If you have ever watched the Michael Powell and Emeric Pressburger classic 'The Life And Death Of Colonel Blimp', you would remember the frenetic comic frenzy of the first fifteen minutes, choreographed like a comic interlude. A squadron of Tommies, all gloriously drunk on wicked mischief, set out to launch a surprise attack on the Turkish bath in London where their Commanding Officer Major General Clive Candy is relaxing in the welcome warmth before the actual drill begins. Much tomfoolery ensu</span>
  <span id="freeText4339501542981988012" style="display:none">If you have ever watched the Michael Powell and Emeric Pressburger classic 'The Life And Death Of Colonel Blimp', you would remember the frenetic comic frenzy of the first fifteen minutes, choreographed like a comic interlude. A squadron of Tommies, all gloriously drunk on wicked mischief, set out to launch a surprise attack on the Turkish bath in London where their Commanding Officer Major General Clive Candy is relaxing in the welcome warmth before the actual drill begins. Much tomfoolery ensues before the film settles down and the actual narrative commences. <br /><br />Now, imagine if Monty Python directed this film and expanded the goofball humour of the first fifteen minutes into a full-length feature packed with more gags and brilliant, blistering British wit and wisecracks than you could digest in one go. Yes, that is what some of this book, the first in the series of wartime memoirs by celebrated British comedian Spike Milligan (who was, coincidentally, the inspiration for Monty Python in the first place with his group act 'The Goon Show'), would feel like: hilarious, anarchic, almost brutally sarcastic, bawdy and guaranteed to leave you in splits. <br /><br />But as I said, it is only some of this book that is hilarious. Don't get me wrong; I laughed, rolled, smiled, shook my head with mock-disbelief and loved all the freaks and weirdos and did not want the splendid comic set-pieces to end. There is a lot of outrageous humour to be found in the pages, some of it is recklessly obscene and deliciously off-the-wall and audacious; there are also crackling one-liners, rambunctious dance evenings that explode into chaos, drunken behaviour, pratfalls during setting up and shifting camp and through it all, you will be nearly tickled to death. <br /><br />But it is hard to be tickled to death when, at the same time, Milligan is also gunning for biting, bitter satirical commentary on the state of the war itself and how it came home to rattle the whole of Britain .There are vividly nightmarish scenes of nerve-wracking despair meshed ingeniously in between the more rib-tickling sequences; there is also a heightened sense of the irreparable damage that destruction and death leave on mere mortals, not least of all the hapless troops marching to war themselves. <br /><br />For instance, read how Milligan describes the tumultous emotions on one of those agonising nights when London is being bombed from the air at night:<br /><br />'We looked at the blaze and it seemed to be getting bigger. I think we all knew it was London. My mother, father and brother were there. I'm not sure how i felt. Helpless, I suppose. Bombardier Edser switched on the BBC Midnight News, but there was no mention of any raid. Lots of the lads from London (we were a London regiment) found it hard to sleep that night. In the dark of our bedrooms, there were attempts at reassurance'. <br /><br />Simple yet effectively stirring and utterly believable because this was exactly how everybody felt in those days. <br /><br />This is, above all, a pitch-perfect and pitch-black satire on war. There are lighter comic digs made at stiff-upper-lipped authority, the abysmal cooking, the futile marches and camping trails that only amount up to idleness, farce and trivial affairs. There are even darker moments towards the end, as the troops set out to sail to Algiers and realise, for the first time, the gruelling experience of bracing through gale at sea, seasickness and even unexpectedly gruesome accidents on the trail that leave them unnerved. <br /><br />Yet, the wonder is that this book, even with its undeniably harsh truths, is so entertaining in the end. Milligan's flippant, conversational tone keeps things wonderfully lively and balances both morbid darkness and cheery camaraderie on an even keel; for all the hilarity and horror, there are also lovely, leisurely moments when the troops celebrate with song, dance and fervent affairs with ladies in between. <br /><br />If you roared with laughter after finishing 'Catch 22', this one comes highly recommended to you, to see the other side of the Atlantic going bonkers over the war long before the actual fighting began.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4339501542981988012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205529697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205529697" />
    <a title="Don S." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5236500-don-s"><img alt="Don S." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483649928p2/5236500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205529697?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Don S." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Don S." href="/user/show/5236500-don-s">Don S.</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_3425398013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3425398013" />
    <a title="Phrodrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67951314-phrodrick"><img alt="Phrodrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545868348p2/67951314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3425398013?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrodrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrodrick" href="/user/show/67951314-phrodrick">Phrodrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780241958094" href="/book/show/14849020-adolf-hitler">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3425398013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6970400164509187662">Since my copy of Spike Milligan’s Adolf Hitler: My Part in His Downfall is on Kindle and to get it out of the way there are some nice drawings throughout the book and they do not show well on a Kindle Viewer. At my side is a paperback copy of Book 4 of his war time memoirs and the photos in it are much crisper, even if page size is only slightly larger.<br/><br/>With that out of the way, my recommendation is that this is better thought of as the war time memoires of a soldier, musician, and humorist and n</span>
  <span id="freeText6970400164509187662" style="display:none">Since my copy of Spike Milligan’s Adolf Hitler: My Part in His Downfall is on Kindle and to get it out of the way there are some nice drawings throughout the book and they do not show well on a Kindle Viewer. At my side is a paperback copy of Book 4 of his war time memoirs and the photos in it are much crisper, even if page size is only slightly larger.<br /><br />With that out of the way, my recommendation is that this is better thought of as the war time memoires of a soldier, musician, and humorist and not as it tends to be sold as the early humor of the leader of BBC radio gag show, The Goon Squad. This being the great Spike Milligan, his humor is foremost, but he is also addressing his demons, and remembering people who became casualties along the way. In some ways I think Adolf Hitler: My Part in His Downfall, makes for a reasonable follow up to the serious Sword of Honor trilogy by Evelyn Waugh. Both begin with an England grossly unprepared for war and depending on outmoded traditions and building a tradition for muddling through. Milligan see the humor in life, and the bitter humor of being in the ranks. Adolf Hitler: My Part in His Downfall also makes for an odd contrast with the American version of early days in the Army. Clearly Gunner Spike never had to deal with an American Recruit Company drill sergeant. <br /><br />Another reason for reading this book from a more serious point of view is that so much of the humor is dated, insider and to a modern ear flat. Absent a major background in The Goon Squad (which I do not have) or other 1950-1980 British radio and television comedy (which I do) it is likely that a lot of this will mean little to even a modern Englishman. Another reviewer speaks of having to look up the regular use of British Army Initials, (RSM is Regimental Sergeant Major, about as close to God as a new recruit is likely to get). Likewise, there are a flow of expressions that may have long since lost currency. Looking things up is pretty much the end of comic timing.<br /><br />That said a soldier is a solder. Horn dogs, given to being slackers, dubious of authority and at once eager and afraid of the dual nature of war, boredom and violence. Book one of Milligan’s memoirs covers the time from his draftee enlistment to deployment to Africa. Dated or not, he captures the feel of his life in the ranks and reflects how his refusal to be overly impressed by rank or be forced into the standard image of a like one, like all soldier.<br /><br />I will be reading more of Spike Milligan. The chuckles are there but there is more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6970400164509187662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_438523860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438523860" />
    <a title="Liesje Leest" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5958296-liesje-leest"><img alt="Liesje Leest" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411981053p2/5958296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438523860?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liesje Leest" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liesje Leest" href="/user/show/5958296-liesje-leest">Liesje Leest</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958296-liesje-leest?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5958296-liesje-leest?shelf=autobiography-biography">autobiography-biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438523860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6804597127079012573">This book is quite different from other soldiers memoirs I've read before (my favorite probably being <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3215477.All_the_Way_to_Berlin_A_Paratrooper_at_War_in_Europe' title='All the Way to Berlin A Paratrooper at War in Europe by James Megellas' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Way to Berlin: A Paratrooper at War in Europe</a>), mostly because it is written in a humorous style. And while at times I enjoyed that style, and had to laugh because of what I read, at other points it came across a little forces. Like the book <i>had</i> to be funny so jokes/funny lines/puns where place in the text when ever possible. Even if it didn't make the book any better.<br/><br/>Also the 'story lin</span>
  <span id="freeText6804597127079012573" style="display:none">This book is quite different from other soldiers memoirs I've read before (my favorite probably being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3215477.All_the_Way_to_Berlin_A_Paratrooper_at_War_in_Europe" title="All the Way to Berlin A Paratrooper at War in Europe by James Megellas" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Way to Berlin: A Paratrooper at War in Europe</a>), mostly because it is written in a humorous style. And while at times I enjoyed that style, and had to laugh because of what I read, at other points it came across a little forces. Like the book <i>had</i> to be funny so jokes/funny lines/puns where place in the text when ever possible. Even if it didn't make the book any better.<br /><br />Also the 'story line' (can one call it a story?) was a bit uncorrelated at times. While reading I would sometimes wonder "what does that have to do with what you just mentioned?" <br /><br />The book has a tone of photo's and drawings which are a nice addition to the text, and fit well with the way the book is written. <br />Although I don't have that much to complain about the book I am only giving it two stars. This is because I didn't really enjoy reading it that much. It's not a bad book, and I can see why people like it, but I don't think I will be picking up the next books in the series any time soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6804597127079012573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3627797572665544652">I read this a long time ago in a galaxy far, far away aka c/o Gerrards Cross library. I enjoyed it then for the jokes and silliness. I still like those moments but I noticed the serious stuff more this time. The last page for example when he talks about two tragedies, lightens it with the story of the Burnt Bum Affair before hitting you with the final line.<br/><br/>It tells the story of Spike Milligan’s war experience. Or at least the early parts of it. The not joining up, the joining up, the band, the c</span>
  <span id="freeText3627797572665544652" style="display:none">I read this a long time ago in a galaxy far, far away aka c/o Gerrards Cross library. I enjoyed it then for the jokes and silliness. I still like those moments but I noticed the serious stuff more this time. The last page for example when he talks about two tragedies, lightens it with the story of the Burnt Bum Affair before hitting you with the final line.<br /><br />It tells the story of Spike Milligan’s war experience. Or at least the early parts of it. The not joining up, the joining up, the band, the chaos of training and preparation, the sex and the boredom. Milligan’s book is one of the few war memoirs to make clear how much sex was going on then. Like now I suppose but with the added knowledge that the person you were shagging might be dead tomorrow. Which is also true if today if you choose to think about. Which you don’t because that way lies melancholy and poetry.<br /><br />Anyway I recommend this book. There are moments of what might be called political correctness but this is Spike Milligan. A man of his time and not. <br /><br />Read it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3627797572665544652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1364716816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364716816" />
    <a title="Jack Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19920958-jack-gibson"><img alt="Jack Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594616503p2/19920958.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364716816?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Gibson" href="/user/show/19920958-jack-gibson">Jack Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/10782887-adolf-hitler">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All interested in WW2, offering you an alternative narrative</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19920958-jack-gibson?shelf=war-conflict">war-conflict</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19920958-jack-gibson?shelf=biographical">biographical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364716816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9301806939002720082">WW2 according to Gunner Terence Alan Milligan offers the reader a very unique, funny yet integral view of his life during and the times that were World War Two.<br/><br/>This book has sheer brilliancy in its ability to allow you to sit back in a chair, laugh and marvel yet sit up straight for its realness to reality all at the same time. For example "In the early days doughnuts were liberally dusted with castor sugar, but as war went on that stopped. War was coming nearer even for doughnuts." <br/><br/>As a man who</span>
  <span id="freeText9301806939002720082" style="display:none">WW2 according to Gunner Terence Alan Milligan offers the reader a very unique, funny yet integral view of his life during and the times that were World War Two.<br /><br />This book has sheer brilliancy in its ability to allow you to sit back in a chair, laugh and marvel yet sit up straight for its realness to reality all at the same time. For example "In the early days doughnuts were liberally dusted with castor sugar, but as war went on that stopped. War was coming nearer even for doughnuts." <br /><br />As a man who reads a lot of historical books, this one stands on a shelf of its own for its approach to writing, which is also greatly aided by accompanying sketches to illustrate points. In the preface, Spike states: "All the salient facts are true, I have garnished some of them in my own manner, but the basic facts are, as I say, true." Further "There were the deaths of some of my friends, and therefore, no matter how funny I tried to make this book, that will always be at the back of my mind: but, were they alive today, they would have been first to join in the laughter, and that laughter was, I'm sure, the key to victory." After all, these men were part of a war where many people would not see the end of it.<br /><br />When reading this book I wanted to jot down quote after quote after quote, but then I realised that picking one or two quotes out doesn't give the book the full justice and chance it deserves because the whole book is quotable...so if you want more-read it good peoples :).<br /><br />The book is written in "...the simple language of the barrack room...", making it more engaging, but just to warn readers who aren't too familiar with WW2 and the lingo and happenings of the day, you may need to look a few bits up.<br /><br />I can't wait to read the next six volumes.<br /><br />A MUST read for anyone interested in WW2 (you will never read another account quite like this) and anyone up for laugh at reality; you will find all emotions stirring...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9301806939002720082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1935384878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1935384878" />
    <a title="PaulD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52697852-pauld"><img alt="PaulD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489590747p2/52697852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1935384878?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PaulD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PaulD" href="/user/show/52697852-pauld">PaulD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935384878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14222230233323942248">"Silence when you speak to an officer" This order was barked out by a sergeant major to Terrance Milligan on reporting to his commanding officer months late due to a slipped disc. This screamed sentence, which left the sergeant major frothing at the mouth was due to Terrance or less formally 'Spike' Milligan saying he new he was late but "I'll fight nights to make it up". This is a war diary like no other, Hitler never stood a chance once Gunner Milligan donned his uniform. I can't remember how </span>
  <span id="freeText14222230233323942248" style="display:none">"Silence when you speak to an officer" This order was barked out by a sergeant major to Terrance Milligan on reporting to his commanding officer months late due to a slipped disc. This screamed sentence, which left the sergeant major frothing at the mouth was due to Terrance or less formally 'Spike' Milligan saying he new he was late but "I'll fight nights to make it up". This is a war diary like no other, Hitler never stood a chance once Gunner Milligan donned his uniform. I can't remember how many times I've read his war books, if you ever want empty seats either side of you on a train or tube read Spikes books you just laugh out loud and people tend not to need those empty seats next to you. If you have read or want to read his books you will be privileged to be a voyeur at the birth of a comic writer of mind blowing importance. No Spike, No Monty Python, yes his tales of barrack life are crude but so so funny. Spike often said that his army days were among the happiest of his life, yet they took a toil on his health a victim of shell shock and the loss of friends in action. If you ever feel down and need a bit of a lift reach for Adolf Hitler: My part in his downfall </span>
  <a data-text-id="14222230233323942248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_143794626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143794626" />
    <a title="Tom M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4676525-tom-m"><img alt="Tom M" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143794626?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom M" href="/user/show/4676525-tom-m">Tom M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143794626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12604341999486728107">An autobiography of Spike Milligan's time in the English army in World War II.<br/><br/>His writings are humorous and sometimes serious anecdotes of his time served in the war. Constantly making wisecracks to his superiors, he passed through his various training duties only by the grace of god and no help from that damned Warsaw Symphony. The anecdotes progress from his time in Eastbourne/Hailsham and end when he'd arrived in Algiers. While in Eastbourne, he'd learned the trumpet and started his lifelong </span>
  <span id="freeText12604341999486728107" style="display:none">An autobiography of Spike Milligan's time in the English army in World War II.<br /><br />His writings are humorous and sometimes serious anecdotes of his time served in the war. Constantly making wisecracks to his superiors, he passed through his various training duties only by the grace of god and no help from that damned Warsaw Symphony. The anecdotes progress from his time in Eastbourne/Hailsham and end when he'd arrived in Algiers. While in Eastbourne, he'd learned the trumpet and started his lifelong love of jazz, and cobbled together a jazz group with other men. They would play often, and even played for some social functions of the army brass. <br /><br />I was interested in this book because of the Milligan name, though I didn't know initially that this was an autobiography. There are some hilarious passages but others are dull; the anecdotes are arranged almost haphazardly in a loose order by event, so the progression of the book is a bit clunky.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12604341999486728107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12318174-emily-von-pfahl?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12318174-emily-von-pfahl?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544958505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3678757601986852258">My best friend suggested this book for our book club, and she in turn, got the recommendation from an interview with Emma Thompson that she read. This book is hysterically funny and poignant at the same time. It clearly demonstrates the concept that war is hours of boredom punctuated by moments of sheer terror. Not surprisingly, some of our more stodgy members of book club didn't find this to be entertaining at all. But then again, they recommend books like Night by Elie Weisel and other depress</span>
  <span id="freeText3678757601986852258" style="display:none">My best friend suggested this book for our book club, and she in turn, got the recommendation from an interview with Emma Thompson that she read. This book is hysterically funny and poignant at the same time. It clearly demonstrates the concept that war is hours of boredom punctuated by moments of sheer terror. Not surprisingly, some of our more stodgy members of book club didn't find this to be entertaining at all. But then again, they recommend books like Night by Elie Weisel and other depressing things. My friend and I, on the other hand, wished Spike Milligan was still alive so we could meet him. A fascinating man to be sure.<br />I was delighted to discover that this was the first in a series of his memoirs, and eagerly went online to check their availability. I was incredibly frustrated by the fact that they are out of print in the states.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3678757601986852258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P17tiFAnS8PpKU6J9ObhEKucymGHa1iX65dtZVYR0luqyqNA2oRQG/8bD5zO+mQn9rOzJ/yhEWdfrvKE59o1bg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

As Head of a reconstituted Liberal Studies Department he has assumed power without authority at the Fenland College of Arts &amp; Technology and the fantasies he now confronts are those of political bigots and reactionary bureaucrats- in addition to his wife\'s enthusiasm for every Organic Alternative under the compost heap and the insistence of his quadruplets on looking at every problem with an unflinching lack of sentimentality. Wilt\'s problems are compounded by nature in the shape of a rose bush, nostalgia, temporary infatuation with a foreign student and the hostility of medical services unwilling to attend to his most urgent needs. But it is only when Wilt becomes the unintentional participant in a terrorist siege that he is forced to find an answer to the problems of power, which have corrupted greater men than he. With a mental ingenuity born of his innate cowardice, Wilt fights for those liberal values which are threatened both by international terrorism and by the sophisticated methods of police anti- terrorist agents. In the confusion that follows, Wilt resumes his dialogue with the unflagging Inspector Flint and is himself subjected to the indignity of a psycho- political profile. Bitingly funny and brilliantly written, THE WILT ALTERNATIVE exposes the farcical anomalies, which have become the social norms of our time.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12426484240547634110\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6340214304547135592">Terence Alan Patrick Seán Milligan, known as Spike, was a comedian, writer and musician. He was of Irish descent, but spent most of his childhood in India and lived most of his later life in England, moving to Australia after retirement. He is famous for his work in The Goon Show, children's poetry and a series of comical autobiographical novels about his experiences serving in the British Army in</span>
  <span id="freeText6340214304547135592" style="display:none">Terence Alan Patrick Seán Milligan, known as Spike, was a comedian, writer and musician. He was of Irish descent, but spent most of his childhood in India and lived most of his later life in England, moving to Australia after retirement. He is famous for his work in The Goon Show, children's poetry and a series of comical autobiographical novels about his experiences serving in the British Army in WWII. Spike Milligan suffered from bipolar disorder, which led to depression and frequent breakdowns, but he will be remembered as a comic genius. His tombstone reads 'I told you I was ill' in Gaelic.</span>

"I'm too young to go," I screamed as Military Policemen dragged me from my pram, clutching a dummy. At Victoria Station the R.T.O. gave me a travel warrant, a white feather and a picture of Hitler marked "This is your enemy." I searched every compartment, but he wasn't on the train. At 4.30, June 2nd, 1940, on a summer's day all mare's tails and blue sky we arrived at Bexhill-on-Sea, where I got off. It wasn't easy. The train didn't stop there.&rdquo;</span>
